O, children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, through its completion, its end has been reached, and through its expositions and declarations, it is clear to me that I have completed it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the manual operation, that is, surgery.
Because the manual operation is widespread in our region and time, it is almost entirely private, to the extent that the knowledge of it is greatly endangered, and its practice is obstructed; and only a few small descriptions remain in the books of the Ancients, which have been misinterpreted and have caused error and hesitation, to the point that understanding of it has been lost and the skill has diminished.
And it seems to me that I can revive it [the manual operation] through the organization of this treatise, following the method of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and so that it may come with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the craft, as it is by adding to the explanation, and by preparing them, which is necessary.
But the reason why a skilled artisan with a practiced hand is not found in this time of ours is that the art of medicine is extensive, and that its practitioner must previously be versed in the science of anatomy, which encompasses the knowledge of the body's organs and their forms, and their connections and separations; and must know the bones, nerves and muscles, their numbers, and their distribution; and the pulsating and still veins, and the locations from which they emerge.
And therefore Hippocrates said that with one name is meant much, but in the practice it is small, and more so in the art of the hand.
But we have already mentioned this in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable in what we have stated about anatomy cannot avoid falling into errors that will lead to the deaths of people, just as I have seen many such cases.  Some are trained in this science, yet depart from it without knowledge or experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician open an scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and cut some of the arteries in her neck, so that a great deal of blood flowed until the woman died in his hands.
And I saw another physician who thought he should remove a stone from a man who was old, and the stone was large.  He went to him and removed the stone with a piece of the bladder, so that the man died on the third day.
And I myself was called to remove that stone, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew beforehand that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving payment from a duke in our land for surgery, and he treated a dark-skinned man whose leg was fractured; and through his ignorance, the physician improperly set the fracture, placing splints and bandages with excessive tightness, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then he (the physician) treated it according to his desires, and then he bound it, and then he left it for some days and commanded that we loosen the bandage.  And it remained like that until the leg and foot became abscessed, and resulted in death.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to loosen the bandage, and tranquility was achieved and he was relieved of his pains.
But meanwhile, corruption had already taken hold in the limb, so I could not stop it, and the corruption continued to spread in the limb until the patient died.
And I saw another physician who opened a cancerous abscess, and it festered for a few days, until the severity of the illness increased with the patient's suffering.
Because the cancerous tumor is purely made of melancholic humor, it is not appropriate to treat it with iron altogether, but rather to target the limb that suffers most from its presence.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you that the operation with the hands be divided into two parts: one is the operation that is associated with health, and the other the work that entails danger in the most serious cases.
And I have already highlighted this throughout this book in which operations are fraught with error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against this and abandon it, lest the pages find a way to speak and discredit you.
Therefore, take your tools with diligence and with God's protection, and your patients with ease and firmness.
And use the best method, through God's grace, aiming for health and laudable success, and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and remove from your arsenal whatever makes you fear, so that your reputation and your name are not tarnished: for it is more important to your glory, and higher in the world, and later to your holiness.
Gualia already said in some of his pronouncements: Do not treat a serious illness, lest you be called bad doctors".
And I have divided this book into three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter, ordered from head to foot, on the forms of instruments and the tools for cauteries, and what is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on cutting and piercing, and cupping, and cauteries, and the extraction of arrows and similar things, all chaptered and ordered according to the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting and similar injuries; a chapter ordered from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments.
It is necessary for me to describe the benefits of this cauterization and its harms, and in what constitution cauterization is forbidden.
Therefore I say that the discussion of the benefits and harms of cauterization is long and drawn out, subtle in its science, and a hidden secret; and already a great multitude of wise men have spoken of it, disagreeing on it, but I will suffice with a small portion of their discussions, fearing to be too lengthy.
And therefore I say that cauterization is beneficial to all constitutions universally, whether with or without material causes, except for two constitutions, which are hot constitutions without material causes.
In the hot and dry constitution with material causes, there is disagreement; for some say that cauterization is helpful in that case, and others say the opposite, that cauterization is not appropriate for an illness characterized by heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat and dryness, and it is inappropriate for a hot and dry illness to be treated with something that is hot and dry.
And those who say the opposite argue that cauterization is beneficial in all hot and dry illnesses affecting the human body, because when you compare the human body and its humours to the constitution of fire, you find the human body to be cold.
And I say, concerning this matter, that experience has shown me this to be true on several occasions.
However, this should not be taken as a final word on the subject by someone who is already skilled and experienced in the practice of cauterization, having learned about the diversity of human constitutions, the nature of illnesses themselves, their causes, their symptoms, and the proper timing for treatment.
But in other constitutions, there is no need for such caution, especially in cold and moist illnesses, for all physicians have agreed upon their treatment and do not disagree about the use of cauterization in those cases.
And know, children, that the secret of healing by cauterization with fire, and its effectiveness, is due to cauterization using fire as a medicine which is more effective, because fire is simple, its effect reaching only the part being cauterized and not harming other connected parts except with minor damage.
However, the action of a burning medicine reaches the parts of the body further away from it, and easily causes a difficult-to-heal illness and substantial harm.
But fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this; rather, it is redundant.  And this is known to us through experience and long study of the art, the truth of causes; therefore I am excused from a lengthy discourse. And if it were not for the fact that this is not appropriate for a book on this matter, the secret of the use of fire, and the method of its operation within the body, and the expelling of diseases, would be demonstrated by a philosophical discourse, which would be more useful to you.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time when cauterization is best, and consider the spring the most favorable time.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harm caused by the passing of time is outweighed by the benefit derived from the cauterization, especially if the cauterization is for painful or necessary ailments, severe and sudden, which cannot tolerate delay, since the fear of greater harm resulting from the passage of time outweighs the minor harm from the cauterization itself.
And this is not understood by you, children, or is not valued by the common people and foolish doctors, which is that a disease cured by cauterization is not always a return to health, and they ignore this consequence.
And the reason is not at all as they believe, for cauterization is only a means of medicine that alters the temperament and dries the moistures which cause the pain.
However, cauterization is superior to other medicine because of its power, the effectiveness of its action, and the greatness of its effect.
And it is possible that the ailment will return at some point in time, according to the temperament of the patient, the location of the illness, the patient's constitution, and the accumulation of superfluities within them, and what they have acquired through their diet and similar causes; however, if the illness for which cauterization was administered is a subtle ailment of a limb with few superfluities and moistures, similar to a toothache and the like, then it is possible that the pain will not return, but this happens with small amounts.
And a common saying is that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, and it is a true statement, not for what they understand by it, for they believe that there is no cure that benefits with medicine or any other treatment before cauterization.
But the opposite is true; the idea that cauterization is the last resort in medicine is only when we have tried other methods of treatment for certain illnesses, and those medicines have not been effective, and finally, cauterization is applied, and it benefits from that. And therefore, cauterization being the last resort in medicine is not according to the understanding of common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients would say that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equivalence of gold and the nobility of its substance.
And they would say that the place where the cauterization is done does not matter, though this is not entirely true, for I have tested this and found that it only holds for some bodies and not others, and cauterization with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said; however, when you do cauterization with gold, it is not entirely clear to you, for it is heated according to the amount that you want by the heat of the gold, and it is prepared to receive cold; and if you add more fire, the gold melts due to the fire, and some pieces fall into the fire, and so the artisan may be harmed by the process.
Therefore, cauterization with iron is done more easily and more properly for the correctness of the operation.
And I have organized this chapter on cauterization according to sections, and I have arranged them from the head to the feet, so that the patient may find what they desire.
The first chapter.
This cauterization is effective against dampness and coldness affecting the brain, the causes of which are twofold:  a cause of phlegm and a multitude of rheumatic fluxes, called cold, running from the head to the eye and ear areas; a multitude of sleeping problems; toothaches and throat pain; and generally all illnesses caused by cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar maladies.
The method of this cauterization is as follows:  first, instruct the patient to be purged with laxative medicine, thoroughly cleansing the head, for three or four nights, according to the patient's strength, age, and custom.
Then instruct them to shave their head, and then position them on a smooth bench with their hands resting on their feet.
And then place the blade of your palm, close to the bridge of the nose, between their eyes. However, when the middle finger has reached the spot, mark the area with a branding iron, and then apply the oiled cautery, the method for which is as follows:
And then apply that [cautery] to the marked spot, in a descending manner, with your hand gradually tightening and turning it.
And then lift your hand slightly and examine the area.  If you see a significant amount of bone exposed, about the size of a grain of millet, then lift your hand, and if not, re-apply the iron, another one if necessary, until you see what I have described.
Then take a bit of salt and dissolve it over the area, and leave it for three days.
Then place a cloth soaked in broth over it and leave it until the scab from the cautery is gone. Then treat the area with a four-herb ointment until it is healed.
And if the wound remains open, the arm should be lifted, for this is better and more beneficial.
And some of them say that the bone should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until some part of the bone tissue is charred.
And then that which is charred of the bone should be scraped off, and then it should be healed.
And others say that with the cautery, one should reach the back, so that it presses hard on the bone until the bone breaks, and this is the method of a small cauterization. And they believe that vapors from the head are released from that location.
And let the wound be kept open for a long time, and then be treated until it is healed and consolidated.
However, I have not seen these two types of cauterization in all cases, but only in some individuals, according to the route of caution; and in my opinion, it is better to preserve health, when possible; for the head is weakened by a disruption of its continuity, just as we have witnessed in other parts of the body, especially when the patient's head is of a fragile nature.
And the first type of cauterization is safer and better in my opinion; and by this method and this work, health is preserved.
Second Chapter.
Of cauterization of the head.
When a chronic and prolonged headache afflicts the patient, and they have used leeches, cupping, head purges, plasters, washes, poultices, and similar remedies, and especially if they have already been cauterized with a cauterization technique that doesn't benefit them, then consider if the patient's head is of strong constitution, not fragile, and is experiencing extreme cold, then one should cauterize with another cauterization technique slightly below the previous one. And then cauterize that area above the patient's temple with a cautery until the inflammation is broken. Incise the inflammation and expose the bone, the quantity of which we have described, and cauterize it with a cautery in the back part of the head, in the area called the *vas* (vein) – and this is the area where a cupping vessel is placed. And ease your hand in doing this, and do not expose the bone, for the patient will experience very great pain different from the pain of all other head cauterizations.
And I will describe this cautery in its place, for the cautery used for cauterizing the temples and the back of the head must be a finer cautery than the one used for cauterizing the middle part of the head; and this is the method for it.
Third Chapter.
Concerning the cauterization of non-ancient migraine.
When, in the head's area, there is persistent or spreading pain extending to the eye, the head should be cleansed with medicines, and the other treatment I have described in my discussion of illnesses should be administered.  If this does not help, cauterization is performed in two ways: either with a sharp, burning medicine, or with iron.
But cauterization with a burning medicine is when you take an onion, squeeze it, and cut the ends off both of its ends. Then, using a sharp lancet, cut the painful area on the temple until a small depression is created beneath the skin, until it is hidden.
Then, press on it with a bandage to constrict the area, and leave it for three hours. Then, remove it and take away the onion, and leave the wound for two or three days, and then apply cotton soaked in butter until the area heals.
And then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines, which I have written in the second treatise on burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron according to this method:  apply fire for cauterization, of which this is the form:
and it is called a 'nail' (or 'clavilh'), because its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it there is a small eminence.
Then place it over the painful area, and hold your hand—so that the surrounding flesh is not burned—and turn the small iron slowly and with speed.
And if the amount burned by the intensity of the cautery is about half of it, then lift your hand to prevent the underlying artery from being burned, so that no blood flow occurs.
Then soak cotton in salt water and place it over the area, and leave it for three days; then place cotton moistened with butter, and then treat with ointment until healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the blade of a knife (like a cautery), and be careful not to cut an artery in this particular, not-ancient, form of migraine.
Fourth Chapter.
Concerning the cauterization of ancient migraine.
When you treat a migraine with what we have described in the previous treatment, and what we have discussed in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment is ineffective, and sometimes the illness prevents the patient from benefiting from what we have previously described - the first cauterization with medicine or with fire - then you should heat the knife cautery until it glows white-hot, then apply it to the pain area in a line of half a finger's length, or as needed;  and place your hand there once, pressing firmly until you cut into the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful not to harm the continuity of the jaw, which is strained by chewing, and that the ligament and nerves that control it are not damaged, and that spasm does not result.
And if it concerns the guarding and caution against blood flow from the severed artery, for there is fear in its severance, especially for one who is ignorant of what they are doing and is not skilled and experienced; and leaves the operation unfinished at the start.
And I will come back to the treatment of accidental blood flow from the artery in its proper manner in its place in this book.
And if you see that this treatment is not sufficient for this ailment, and the patient's condition appears tolerable, cauterize the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, apply the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery constriction with a cautery having two blades; this is a better and more beneficial cauterization.
Chapter 5.
Concerning the cauterization of earaches.
When an earache is caused by cold and is treated with laxatives and the other remedies mentioned in the division, and the pain persists, then apply the cautery, and this is the one called *puncta*, whose shape is as follows:
And then, apply the heated cautery point by point around the entire ear, moving in a circular motion, or in sections if the pain is localized in a specific area. Move the cautery along the base of the ear slowly, after marking the location with a probe.
And if the cautery has ten points across the whole ear, use that many, and then treat the affected areas until they are healed.
Chapter 6.
On the cauterization of tumors.
Tumors that are cured by cauterization are only of the types that arise from phlegm, as we have stated in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the type caused by dryness or nerve spasm.
When you treat that type of tumor with poultices, purges, and remedies, and your treatment is ineffective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, a second one a little below the temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the diseased area, for softening occurs only on the area that appears healthy.
And the method of cauterization is to cauterize with the cautery at the right of the ear's extremity, slightly above the corner of the head, and another one at the temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the index finger, and hold the cautery until the affected area has been burned to half its thickness.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of surgical instrument, the form of which is described before. However, it is even more subtle than that which you see; and it is necessary to cut away some of the superfluous thickness in that area.
And then treat the area with what was previously described until it is healed.
Chapter 7.
On the cauterization of old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is longstanding and you have treated it with what we have said, and you do not see improvement in the treatment, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize with four cauteries: on all the corners of the head; and with a cautery on the middle part of the head, as we have said; and with a cautery on the jaw. And the method of cauterization is done as described above.
And it has already been cauterized on the opening of the stomach; and further back; and then it should be treated with what follows.
Chapter 8.
Concerning cauterization for forgetfulness caused by flame.
Large jars and pills, which cleanse the brain, should be given to the patient at the beginning.
And then shave the patient's entire head and apply a plaster of ceter, as described in the treatise on plasters, to their temples.
And apply that several times, for that is a form of cautery. And do this according to the same order that I have already stated.
And so, if that is a good cure, then do this.  But if not, then make three cauteries on the back part of their head, descending from the highest part of the head to the lowest part of the neck. And place the width of a finger between each cautery, and then treat the cautery with whatever was previously mentioned.
However, if the application is slight and the patient tolerates it, then make the cautery in the middle; and if there is greater need, then cauterize that area over the two horns.
Then treat it until it is healed; and let the cautery be oiled, according to the form previously given.
Chapter 9.
Concerning cauterization for paralysis and the softening of the entire body.
You should proceed with cleansing the head with herbs and as previously described; then shave the patient's head, and then cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on each horn of the head, and with a cautery on the back part of the head, and with three cauteries on the spinal vertebrae of the neck.
And if, in the illness of softening of the body, the patient is particularly weak and the illness is severe, then cauterize with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and continuously with a cautery until the pain has lessened significantly, and lift your hand. And then treat him until he is healed, and this should be an olive oil cautery.
Chapter 10.
Of cauterization for epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized unless the epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to modify his brain at the beginning, using herbs and other treatments we have described in the division when the patient is seriously ill and tolerates the use of strong medicines.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate the medicines, then administer remedies and mastigators that modify the brain, beforehand for several days, with the proper preparation of foods.
And then shave the patient's head, and then cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head according to the previous method, and with another cautery at the back of the head, and cauterize on each temple (horn of the head). And if the illness is severe and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize the patient with the cauteries I have described, having simultaneously paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
Let the cautery be olive-shaped, as previously described.
But if the patient is a child, then use a gentle cautery according to this method.
Chapter 11.
On the cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humidity and a large flame, then cauterize it with the cauteries that we have described in the previous paralysis section.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity tending towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him to drink what cleanses his brain, according to what has been previously stated in the division.
Then shave the patient's head, and then carefully apply a properly made torquet to it around the circumference, and then place it over the middle of the head.
And the patient should be seated securely, and held firmly in all parts.
And then apply a liniment; and it is better to use an old sheep's wool. And heat that over a fire with a measured, moderate heat, which the said person can tolerate when it is placed upon them. And then pour it onto the center of their head, inside the circle, and leave it until it has cooled.
And do this to the patient once a week, with the rest of their treatment, until they are healed; or if you wish, cauterize that area by making small points according to their ability, holding the hand with a cautery that is thus ordered: this is a type of cautery that moistens the brain equally.
And then place that cloth soaked in wool or hen's grease.
Chapter 12.
Of the cauterization of descending water in the head.
When you have determined the beginning of water in the head by the signs I have described in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink that which will dry the head, and protect it from all moisture.
And make him sweat in a bath for several days.
And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle part of the head; and then cauterize it with two cauteries on both temples if the beginning of water-disease is in both ears, or on one side if the beginning of the water-disease is in one ear.
Cut with cauteries all the veins and arteries which are below the scalp; and let the cauteries be of that length in the width of the temples.
And watch out for blood flow when it is cauterized; and if you see blood flow from it, stop it with any medicine that is possible for you.
And I will come with the skill that is in the extraction of arteries and with the excision of those and the precaution against blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck below two bones with two cauteries directly applied.
Chapter 13.
Of the cauterization of old sores/wounds.
When sores on the face are old, persistent, and run through the veins and arteries visible on the outside of the head, and it is verified that this is due to cold phlegmatic superfluities, then cauterize it with the cautery we described in the chapter on hot water compresses for sores, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries on the neck below the temples, and with two cauteries on the neck below the bones. And if more treatment is needed, then cauterize along the entire edge of the sore on the eyebrow's extremity with a small cautery.
Chapter 14.
Of the cauterization of nasal discharge/foul odor.
If your treatment using the methods we discussed is ineffective, then prepare and give the patient a potion to drink for three nights; then shave the patient's head and cauterize it with a middling cautery and an olive cautery. And then cauterize it with a clove cautery, using two cauteries on the two eyebrows below the hair, a small one.
And be careful not to set it on fire.
And this is the method for the clove cautery.
Chapter 15.
Of cauterization for softening the eyelids of the eyes.
When the eyelid is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery using this lunar cautery; and this is its method:
And if you, cauterize that slightly on both eyebrows, using two cauteries on each spot, and keep them spaced from the temples. And the length of each cautery should be according to the size of the eyebrow.
And do not press your hand with the cautery too hard, but just enough so that the third part of the eyelid is adhered.
Chapter 16.
Of cauterization of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are turned inwards and the eye is inflamed.
When the hairs of the eye are turned inward, causing inflammation of the eye, cauterization in such cases is done in two ways: either with a cautery iron or with a burning medicine.
If with a cautery of fire, instruct the patient beforehand to shave the hairs as those who clean them, until they are lengthened and straightened; and if the inflammation is near the roots of the hair, then you should press the patient's eyes with a bandage so they don't move until the hair has grown back.
So, once the hairs are grown back and straightened, then place the patient's head on your lap, and gently apply a cautery to the eyelid of their eye using a probe, whose shape should be similar to a myrtle leaf, starting the cautery near the hairs.
And then place cotton soaked in egg white or in a ptilli mucilage over the eye.
And then apply the cautery, of which this is its form/shape.
And then cauterize, little by little, in several applications, over the area you marked, until the surface of the inflamed area, which is roughly the shape of a myrtle leaf, is completely charred.
The sign of successful treatment is that you see the eyelid drawn together and the hairs rising towards the puncture in the eye.
And then lift your hand and leave it for three days, and then place cotton with a border over it until the scab has healed. And then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
But if, due to some cause, hair growth returns near the origin and the eyelid softens, then apply the cautery again in the same manner as you did at first.
But if the hairs are under the eyelid, then cauterize it until they are raised to their natural position, healed, and the hairs no longer irritate the eye.
But the cautery with burning medicine that you prescribe to the patient involves pulling the hairs out until they are elongated and healed, and then a piece of cloth shaped like a myrtle leaf should be applied.
And then take known herb and fresh living vinegar, or whatever is appropriate, and thoroughly mix these ingredients quickly so they don't get cold.  Then spread this mixture onto the cloth shaped like a myrtle leaf, and place this over the affected eye(s).  Place a cloth soaked in albumen of an egg under the eye, and the patient's head should be supported.
And press the cloth onto the medicine, pressing it gently, but do not remove it until the patient feels the medicine's burning sensation, for the burning sensation is like that of fire.
And thus, as long as the patient feels the burning sensation, leave the medicine in place.  Then, when the burning sensation stops, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.  Then consider if the eyelid is now raised as it should be, without constriction from fire or incision. If so, it is well done. If not, return to applying the medicine to the affected area and continue until the healing is complete, and the eye is closed.
Then apply a cloth over the area until the burn's inflammation has subsided, and then treat it with a healing ointment or other appropriate remedy until it is healed.
It is necessary for you, during your treatment, to carefully watch that nothing of the medicine gets into the eye.  And if after a few days the eyelid becomes softened and something of the hair or skin gets into the eye, then reapply your medicine to the softened area of the eyelid, just as you did at the beginning, and continue until it heals.
And this is the method of using myrtle leaf.
Know that human eyes differ in size and thus the treatment for their condition is adjusted accordingly.
And the path to recovery for the one who studies this art will not be hidden.
Chapter 17.
Of the cauterization of a fistula in the tear duct of the eye.
When you treat a fistula, as we have discussed in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment doesn't work, then you should cauterize it in this way: instruct the patient to rest their head on your lap, and have an assistant hold the patient's head between your hands, so that it is neither moved nor agitated by their head movements.
And then place a piece of cotton, soaked in egg white or phlli gum, over their eye.
And then heat the cautery, whose form is:
which should be hollow, like the shape of a reed or a hawk's feather, at the end from which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, let it penetrate to the other end. And if you wish, let it be slender, like a probe.
However, the one that is hollow is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and drain and dry it. And if it is not open, then open it and remove the pus from it.
And then place the heated cautery on it, and hold your hand a short distance from the cautery, near the nostril, so that your hand or the patient is not disturbed, and then place the cautery on the ulcer and cauterize it.
And therefore, if at the beginning your cautery penetrates to the bone, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if necessary; and leave it thus for three days, and then apply a bandage with lint and surround it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
But if more than ten days have passed and it is not healed, then apply a sharp, corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and is scraped as appropriate in your chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some earlier practitioners described:  Apply pressure to the fistula opening and make it wider. Then place a thin piece of lead, shaped as is described, into that opening; hold it in place with your hand firmly, so that the molten lead does not enter the wound; you should apply a bandage soaked in egg white or water to the patient's wound, as the lead will adhere to the fistula opening and heal it, bringing remarkable recovery.
And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization and treatment we have described, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer a perforation of the nose and reduce the fistula back into the nasal passage, according to its proper location.
Chapter 18.
Concerning the cauterization of a fissure in the pot/cavity.
Often fissures occur in the lips, especially in the lips of children.

Of cauterization of fistulas in the mouth.

Chapter 20.
Of cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are decayed, and treatment with medicines does not help, then place the patient's head on your lap. Hold your hand there for a short time, so that the patient feels the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth.
And then remove your hand, and repeat the cauterization a few times, as desired.
Then have the patient fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, then spit it out.  For the decayed tooth is sealed, the softened gums are strengthened, and the corrupt moisture is dried out.
Chapter 21.
Of cauterization for toothache.
When toothache is caused by cold, or there is cold or a worm in it, or you do not consider medicine a cure, then cauterization in that case is done in two ways: either with a cow's dung cautery, or with fire.
Cauterization with dung is done by taking cow dung, boiling it in an iron pot, then taking a piece of cloth, wrapping it around the end of a probe, dipping it into the boiled dung, and quickly placing it on the aching tooth until it is cooled.
And repeat this several times until the heat's effect reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cloth in the aforementioned dung, place it on the aching tooth, and place the heated iron upon it until the iron reaches the hollow of the tooth.
However, cauterization with fire is that you use a heated iron or bronze cannula, ensuring that its thickness is sufficient to prevent the heat from reaching the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery, shaped appropriately, and place it on the tooth, holding it until the cautery cools; repeat this several times, as the pain will either cease that day or the next.
And it is necessary that, during the application of the cautery, the patient fill their mouth with good dung and hold it for an hour, then spit it out; and this is the method of cauterization.

Chapter 28.

Chapter 29.

And the elevation of the arm should be such that it extends along the length of the body, so that cauterizations are made along the width of the body.
Then introduce the two jets of fire, quite intensely, into that space, so that they penetrate the arm on the other side.
Then remove the cautery; and thus four cauteries have been made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three jets of fire.
And then you should treat the cautery, as it has stopped emitting fire for too many days, for this is more important than the other preceding actions in the cure.

Chapter 45.
